			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">World economy</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20_Largest_economies_pie_chart.pdf" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/20_Largest_economies_pie_chart.pdf/page1-310px-20_Largest_economies_pie_chart.pdf.jpg" width="310" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/20_Largest_economies_pie_chart.pdf/page1-465px-20_Largest_economies_pie_chart.pdf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/20_Largest_economies_pie_chart.pdf/page1-620px-20_Largest_economies_pie_chart.pdf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1362" data-file-height="1318" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20_Largest_economies_pie_chart.pdf" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
20 Largest economies pie chart</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <b>world economy</b> or <b>global economy</b> is the <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economy</a> of the world, considered as the international exchange of goods and services that is expressed in monetary units of account (money).<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> In some contexts, the two terms are distinguished: the "international" or "global economy" being measured separately and distinguished from <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">national</a> economies while the "world economy" is simply an aggregate of the separate countries' measurements. Beyond the minimum standard concerning value in production, use, and exchange the definitions, representations, models, and valuations of the world economy vary widely. It is inseparable from the geography and ecology of Earth.</p>
<p>It is common to limit questions of the world economy exclusively to <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">human economic activity</a>, and the world economy is typically judged in monetary terms, even in cases in which there is no efficient market to help valuate certain goods or services, or in cases in which a lack of independent research or government cooperation makes establishing figures difficult. Typical examples are <a href="/wiki/Illegal_drug_trade" title="Illegal drug trade">illegal drugs</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Underground_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Underground economy">black market goods</a>, which by any standard are a part of the world economy, but for which there is by definition no legal market of any kind.</p>
<p>However, even in cases in which there is a clear and efficient market to establish a monetary value, economists do not typically use the current or official exchange rate to translate the monetary units of this market into a single unit for the world economy, since exchange rates typically do not closely reflect <a href="/wiki/World" title="World">worldwide</a> value, for example in cases where the volume or price of transactions is closely regulated by the government.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C2%B4World_Bank,_icp_2011_gdp_ppp_world_share.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%C2%B4World_Bank%2C_icp_2011_gdp_ppp_world_share.png/310px-%C2%B4World_Bank%2C_icp_2011_gdp_ppp_world_share.png" width="310" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%C2%B4World_Bank%2C_icp_2011_gdp_ppp_world_share.png/465px-%C2%B4World_Bank%2C_icp_2011_gdp_ppp_world_share.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%C2%B4World_Bank%2C_icp_2011_gdp_ppp_world_share.png/620px-%C2%B4World_Bank%2C_icp_2011_gdp_ppp_world_share.png 2x" data-file-width="2684" data-file-height="1926" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C2%B4World_Bank,_icp_2011_gdp_ppp_world_share.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
World share of GDP (<a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a>) (<a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, 2011).<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rather, market valuations in a local currency are typically translated to a single monetary unit using the idea of <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power</a>. This is the method used below, which is used for estimating worldwide economic activity in terms of <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">real</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US dollars</a> or euros. However, the world economy can be evaluated and expressed in many more ways. It is unclear, for example, how many of the world's <a href="/wiki/World_population" title="World population">7.13 billion people</a> have most of their economic activity reflected in these valuations.</p>
<p>As of 2015, the following 13 countries or regions have reached an economy of at least US$2 trillion by GDP in nominal or PPP terms: <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, and <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_world_economic_league_table_of_largest_economies_in_the_world_by_GDP_and_share_of_global_economic_growth">Current world economic league table of largest economies in the world by GDP and share of global economic growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Current world economic league table of largest economies in the world by GDP and share of global economic growth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following two tables list the twenty largest economies by GDP (Nominal), twenty largest economies by GDP (<a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a>), and the twenty economies with the largest shares of global economic growth from 2014 to 2015. Members of the <a href="/wiki/G-20_major_economies" class="mw-redirect" title="G-20 major economies">G-20 major economies</a> are in bold.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twenty_largest_economies_in_the_world_by_nominal_GDP">Twenty largest economies in the world by nominal GDP</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Twenty largest economies in the world by nominal GDP">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_IMF_ranked_countries_by_historical_GDP_(nominal)" class="mw-redirect" title="List of IMF ranked countries by historical GDP (nominal)">List of IMF ranked countries by historical GDP (nominal)</a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twenty_Largest_Economies_in_the_World_by_PPP_GDP_.28IMF_and_CIA_World_Factbook.29">Twenty Largest Economies in the World by PPP GDP (IMF and CIA World Factbook)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Twenty Largest Economies in the World by PPP GDP (IMF and CIA World Factbook)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following is a list of twenty largest economies by GDP (PPP) at a specific year according to the <a href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" class="mw-redirect" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: left">
<tr>
<th>Rank</th>
<th>1980</th>
<th>1985</th>
<th>1990</th>
<th>1995</th>
<th>2000</th>
<th>2005</th>
<th>2010</th>
<th>2015</th>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistical_indicators">Statistical indicators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Statistical indicators">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> (GWP) (<a href="/wiki/Gross_world_product" title="Gross world product">gross world product</a>):</b> (purchasing power parity exchange rates) – $59.38 trillion (2005 est.), $51.48 trillion (2004), $23 trillion (2002)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> (GWP) (<a href="/wiki/Gross_world_product" title="Gross world product">gross world product</a>):</b><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> <b>(market exchange rates) – $60.69 trillion (2008)</b></li>
<li><b>GDP – real growth rate:</b> 3.2% (2008), 3.1% p.a. (2000–07), 2.4% p.a. (1990–99), 3.1% p.a. (1980–89)</li>
<li><b>GDP – per capita:</b> purchasing power parity – $9,300, €7,500 (2005 est.), $8,200, €6,800 (92) (2003), $7,900, €5,000 (2002)</li>
<li><b>World <a href="/wiki/Median" title="Median">median</a> income</b>: purchasing power parity $1,041, €950 (1993)<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>GDP – composition by sector:</b> agriculture: 4%; industry: 32%; services: 64% (2004 est.)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">Inflation</a> rate (consumer prices):</b> <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed countries</a> 1% to 4% typically; <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a> 5% to 60% typically; national inflation rates vary widely in individual cases, from declining prices in <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Japan" title="Economy of Japan">Japan</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hyperinflation" title="Hyperinflation">hyperinflation</a> in several <a href="/wiki/Third_world" class="mw-redirect" title="Third world">Third World</a> countries (2003)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Derivative_(finance)" title="Derivative (finance)">Derivatives</a> OTC outstanding notional amount</b>: $601 trillion (Dec 2010) (<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.bis.org/statistics/otcder/dt1920a.pdf">[5]</a>)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Derivative_(finance)" title="Derivative (finance)">Derivatives</a> exchange traded outstanding notional amount</b>: $82 trillion (June 2011) (<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.bis.org/publ/qtrpdf/r_qa1109.pdf#page=136">[6]</a>)</li>
<li><b>Global <a href="/wiki/Debt" title="Debt">debt</a> issuance</b>: $5.187 trillion, €3 trillion (2004), $4.938 trillion, €3.98 trillion (2003), $3.938 trillion (2002) (<a href="/wiki/Thomson_Financial_League_Tables" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomson Financial League Tables">Thomson Financial League Tables</a>)</li>
<li><b>Global <a href="/wiki/Stock" title="Stock">equity</a> issuance</b>: $505 billion, €450 billion (2004), $388 billion. €320 billion (2003), $319 billion, €250 trillion (2002) (<a href="/wiki/Thomson_Financial_League_Tables" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomson Financial League Tables">Thomson Financial League Tables</a>)</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">Unemployment</a> rate:</b> 8.7% (2009 est.). 30% (2007 est.) combined unemployment and <a href="/wiki/Underemployment" title="Underemployment">underemployment</a> in many non-industrialized countries; developed countries typically 4%–12% unemployment.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industries">Industries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Industries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b>Industrial production growth rate:</b> 3% (2002 est.)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b>Yearly electricity – production:</b> 21,080,878 GWh (2011 est.),<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> 15,850,000 GWh (2003 est.), 14,850,000 GWh (2001 est.)</li>
<li><b>Yearly electricity – consumption:</b> 14,280,000 GWh (2003 est.), 13,930,000 GWh (2001 est.)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">Oil</a> – production:</b> 79,650,000&#160;bbl/d (12,663,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) (2003 est.), 75,460,000 barrels per day (11,997,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) (2001)</li>
<li><b>Oil – consumption:</b> 80,100,000&#160;bbl/d (12,730,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) (2003 est.), 76,210,000 barrels per day (12,116,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) (2001)</li>
<li><b>Oil – proved reserves:</b> 1.025 trillion barrel (163&#160;km³) (2001 est.)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">Natural gas</a> – production:</b> 3,366&#160;km³ (2012 est.),<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> 2,569&#160;km³ (2001 est.)</li>
<li><b>Natural gas – consumption:</b> 2,556&#160;km³ (2001 est.)</li>
<li><b>Natural gas – proved reserves:</b> 161,200&#160;km³ (1 January 2002)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cross-border">Cross-border</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Cross-border">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b>Yearly exports:</b> $12.4 trillion, €11.05 trillion (2009 est.)</li>
<li><b>Exports – commodities:</b> the whole range of industrial and agricultural goods and services</li>
<li><b>Exports – partners:</b> US 12.7%, Germany 7.1%, China 6.2%, France 4.4%, Japan 4.2%, UK 4.1% (2008)</li>
<li><b>Yearly imports:</b> $12.29 trillion, €10.95 trillion (2009 est.)</li>
<li><b>Imports – commodities:</b> the whole range of industrial and agricultural goods and services</li>
<li><b>Imports – partners:</b> China 10.3%, Germany 8.6%, US 8.1%, Japan 5% (2008)</li>
<li><b>Debt – external:</b> $56.9 trillion, €40 trillion (31 December 2009 est.)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gift_economy">Gift economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Gift economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b>Yearly economic aid – recipient:</b> net <a href="/wiki/Official_Development_Assistance" class="mw-redirect" title="Official Development Assistance">Official Development Assistance</a> (ODA) of $135.2 billion (2014)<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Telephones – main lines in use:</b> 843,923,500 (2007)<br />
4,263,367,600 (2008)</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Telephones – mobile cellular:</b> 3,300,000,000 (Nov. 2007)<sup id="cite_ref-reuters50_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters50-17">[17]</a></sup></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Internet_Service_Providers" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet Service Providers">Internet Service Providers</a> (ISPs):</b> 10,350 (2000 est.)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> users:</b> 3,079,339,857 (December 31, 2014 <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.internetworldstats.com">[7]</a>), 360,985,492 (December 31, 2000<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Transportation infrastructure worldwide includes:</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Airports" class="mw-redirect" title="Airports">Airports</a></b>
<ul>
<li>Total: 41,821 (2013)<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Roadway" class="mw-redirect" title="Roadway">Roadways</a></b> (in kilometres)
<ul>
<li>Total: 32,345,165&#160;km</li>
<li>Paved: 19,403,061&#160;km</li>
<li>Unpaved: 12,942,104&#160;km (2002)</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Railways">Railways</a></b>
<ul>
<li>Total: 1,122,650&#160;km includes about 190,000 to 195,000&#160;km of electrified routes of which 147,760&#160;km are in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, 24,509&#160;km in the <a href="/wiki/Far_East" title="Far East">Far East</a>, 11,050&#160;km in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, 4,223&#160;km in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, and 4,160&#160;km in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (December 2016)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata">– <a href="/wiki/Talk:World_economy#If_it.27s_4000_km_from_New_York_to_Los_Angeles.2C_it.27s_unlikely_there_is_only_4160_km_of_railway_in_North_America." title="Talk:World economy">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b>World military expenditure in 2012:</b> estimated to $1.756 trillion <sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Military expenditures – percent of <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>:</b> roughly 2% of gross world product (1999).</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_studies">Economic studies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_economy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economic studies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>To promote exports, many government agencies publish on the web economic studies by sector and country. Among these agencies include the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Commercial_Service" title="United States Commercial Service">USCS</a> (US DoC) and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Agricultural_Service" title="Foreign Agricultural Service">FAS</a> (USDA) in the United States, <a href="/wiki/Export_Development_Canada" title="Export Development Canada">EDC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_and_Agri-Food_Canada" title="Agriculture and Agri-Food Canada">AAFC</a> in Canada, <a href="/wiki/Ubifrance" title="Ubifrance">Ubifrance</a> in France, <a href="/wiki/UKTI" class="mw-redirect" title="UKTI">UKTI</a> in the UK, <a href="/wiki/HKTDC" class="mw-redirect" title="HKTDC">HKTDC</a> and <a href="/wiki/JETRO" class="mw-redirect" title="JETRO">JETRO</a> in Asia, <a href="/wiki/Austrade" title="Austrade">Austrade</a> and <a href="/wiki/NZTE" class="mw-redirect" title="NZTE">NZTE</a> in Oceania. Through Partnership Agreements, The Federation of International Trade Associations publishes studies from several of these agencies (USCS, FAS, AAFC, UKTI, HKTDC), as well as other non-governmental organizations on its website <a href="/wiki/GlobalTrade.net" title="GlobalTrade.net">GlobalTrade.net</a>.</p>
